# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Configuration Hot-Reload Patterns Across K8s and Prometheus

## Your Task

Find Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes and prometheus/prometheus that implement configuration hot-reload (no process restart): the file watcher setup, the config diff detection, and the atomic config swap that applies new config without dropping connections.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

```json

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

65-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive `answer.json` file at `/workspace/answer.json` that documents the configuration hot-reload patterns found in both repositories.

## Summary of Findings

### **Kubernetes (kubernetes/kubernetes)**
1. **File Watcher**: `pkg/util/filesystem/watcher.go:WatchUntil()` - Combines fsnotify with periodic polling
2. **Config Diff**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/encryptionconfig/controller/controller.go` - SHA256 hash-based detection with TOCTOU protection
3. **Atomic Swap**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/encryptionconfig/config.go:DynamicTransformers.Set()` - Uses `atomic.Value` with grace period for in-flight requests
4. **Secondary Pattern**: `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` - Authorization config reload using `atomic.Pointer`

### **Prometheus (prometheus/prometheus)**
1. **File Watcher**: `cmd/prometheus/main.go` - Time-based polling + fsnotify in `discovery/file/file.go`
2. **Config Diff**: `config/reload.go:GenerateChecksum()` - SHA256 hashing of main config + all referenced rule/scrape files
3. **Atomic Swap**: `cmd/prometheus/main.go:reloadConfig()` → `scrape/manager.go:ApplyConfig()` - Sequential ordered reload across all consumers with parallel scrape pool updates

### **Key Pattern Differences**
- **Kubernetes**: Lock-free reads with `atomic.Value`, explicit grace periods, health checks before swap
- **Prometheus**: Lock-protected sections, ordered reload sequence, parallel pool reload with concurrency limits

Both achieve the goal of updating configuration without dropping connections by ensuring old resources complete their work before being released.

File Watcher Setup (pkg/util/filesystem/watcher.go:WatchUntil)**\\nThe `WatchUntil()` function provides a callback-based filesystem watcher that combines fsnotify for event-driven updates with periodic polling as a fallback. It watches a specified file path and invokes an event handler whenever a change is observed or a poll interval elapses. This dual approach ensures file changes are detected reliably even if fsnotify encounters errors.\\n\\n**2. Config Diff Detection (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/encryptionconfig/controller/controller.go)**\\nThe `DynamicEncryptionConfigContent` controller implements a rate-limited queue pattern (via Kubernetes workqueue). It polls for changes using `EncryptionConfigFileChangePollDuration` (default 1 minute) and detects configuration changes by comparing SHA256 hashes:\\n- `processEncryptionConfig()` first checks if the file hash has changed before attempting to load\\n- If hash differs, it loads the new configuration and validates it\\n- After successful load, it compares hashes again (TOCTOU protection) to ensure the config is truly new\\n- Only if both checks show a difference does it proceed with the swap\\n\\nHash computation is done via `GetEncryptionConfigHash()` in config.go:556, which reads the file and computes `sha256:hexdigest`.\\n\\n**3. Atomic Config Swap (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/encryptionconfig/config.go)**\\nThe `DynamicTransformers` struct uses `atomic.Value` (line 923) to achieve lock-free reads. The `Set()` method (lines 974-998):\\n- Creates a new `transformTracker` struct containing the new transformers and health check\\n- Atomically swaps the old tracker for the new one using `atomic.Value.Swap()` (line 989)\\n- After swap, all new requests immediately use the new transformers (no locks held)\\n- Old transformers are closed asynchronously after a grace period (`kmsCloseGracePeriod`), allowing in-flight requests to complete\\n\\nThe reload workflow is orchestrated by the controller's `Run()` method which calls through `processEncryptionConfig()` \u2192 `validateNewTransformersHealth()` \u2192 `dynamicTransformers.Set()`, ensuring new transformers are healthy before swapping.\\n\\n**Authorization Config Reload (pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go)**\\nA parallel pattern is used for authorization configuration:\\n- `runReload()` uses `filesystem.WatchUntil()` with a configurable `reloadInterval`\\n- `checkFile()` compares file contents byte-by-byte and validates the parsed configuration\\n- Uses `atomic.Pointer[authorizerResolver]` to atomically swap the entire authorizer chain via `Store()` (line 248)\\n\\n### Prometheus: Configuration Hot-Reload with Auto-Detection\\n\\nPrometheus implements configuration hot-reload triggered by both manual signals (SIGHUP, /-/reload API) and automatic change detection:\\n\\n**1. File Watcher Setup (discovery/file/file.go)**\\nThe file discovery component uses `fsnotify.NewWatcher()` to watch configuration files. In cmd/prometheus/main.go, the reload handler monitors for file changes via `time.Tick()` at intervals specified by `--config.auto-reload-interval` (default 30s).\\n\\n**2. Config Diff Detection (config/reload.go:GenerateChecksum)**\\nThe `GenerateChecksum()` function computes a SHA256 hash covering:\\n- The main configuration file content\\n- All referenced rule files (matched via glob patterns from `rule_files` config)\\n- All referenced scrape config files (matched via glob patterns from `scrape_config_files` config)\\n- File paths and contents are hashed in a deterministic order\\n\\nThe reload loop in cmd/prometheus/main.go (lines 1313-1330) compares checksums at each interval and only proceeds with reload if `currentChecksum != checksum`.\\n\\n**3. Atomic Config Swap (cmd/prometheus/main.go:reloadConfig + scrape/manager.go:ApplyConfig)**\\nThe `reloadConfig()` function (lines 1600-1645) performs sequential reloads of all configuration consumers via the `reloaders` slice:\\n- Parses the new configuration using `config.LoadFile()`\\n- Iterates through reloaders in order: scrape manager, rule manager, discovery manager, etc.\\n- Each reloader's `ApplyConfig()` method handles atomic updates\\n\\nThe scrape manager's `ApplyConfig()` (scrape/manager.go:279) demonstrates the swap pattern:\\n- Takes exclusive lock on `mtxScrape`\\n- Validates all new scrape configurations\\n- For each pool, determines if it needs reload by comparing with `reflect.DeepEqual(sp.config, cfg)`\\n- Spawns goroutines to reload pools in parallel (limited by `runtime.GOMAXPROCS(0)`)\\n- Deletes pools removed from configuration\\n- Unlocks and waits for all reload goroutines to complete\\n- Old scrape pools are stopped cleanly while new ones start, and the reload handler invokes discovery manager to fetch new targets\\n\\nThe reload callback (line 1277) updates metrics and notifications based on success/failure. If reload fails, existing configuration remains in use and is not updated.\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n**Kubernetes** emphasizes:\\n- Lock-free reads using `atomic.Value` for zero-impact request path during reload\\n- Grace period for closing old resources, allowing in-flight requests to complete\\n- Health checking of new transformers before swapping\\n\\n**Prometheus** emphasizes:\\n- Deterministic multi-file checksums including rule and scrape config files\\n- Ordered reload sequence across multiple configuration consumers\\n- Parallel reload of scrape pools with concurrency limiting\\n- Clean cascade through discovery manager to fetch new targets\\n\\nBoth use polling with configurable intervals as the primary change detection mechanism, with fsnotify as an optional event-driven enhancement.\"\n}\n",
